     100             : 
     101             : /* Return the smallest scalar part of STMT_INFO.
     102             :    This is used to determine the vectype of the stmt.  We generally set the
     103             :    vectype according to the type of the result (lhs).  For stmts whose
     104             :    result-type is different than the type of the arguments (e.g., demotion,
     105             :    promotion), vectype will be reset appropriately (later).  Note that we have
     106             :    to visit the smallest datatype in this function, because that determines the
     107             :    VF.  If the smallest datatype in the loop is present only as the rhs of a
     108             :    promotion operation - we'd miss it.
     109             :    Such a case, where a variable of this datatype does not appear in the lhs
     110             :    anywhere in the loop, can only occur if it's an invariant: e.g.:
     111             :    'int_x = (int) short_inv', which we'd expect to have been optimized away by
     112             :    invariant motion.  However, we cannot rely on invariant motion to always
     113             :    take invariants out of the loop, and so in the case of promotion we also
     114             :    have to check the rhs.
     115             :    LHS_SIZE_UNIT and RHS_SIZE_UNIT contain the sizes of the corresponding
     116             :    types.  */

    1504             : 
    1505             : /* Function vect_enhance_data_refs_alignment
    1506             : 
    1507             :    This pass will use loop versioning and loop peeling in order to enhance
    1508             :    the alignment of data references in the loop.
    1509             : 
    1510             :    FOR NOW: we assume that whatever versioning/peeling takes place, only the
    1511             :    original loop is to be vectorized.  Any other loops that are created by
    1512             :    the transformations performed in this pass - are not supposed to be
    1513             :    vectorized.  This restriction will be relaxed.
    1514             : 
    1515             :    This pass will require a cost model to guide it whether to apply peeling
    1516             :    or versioning or a combination of the two.  For example, the scheme that
    1517             :    intel uses when given a loop with several memory accesses, is as follows:
    1518             :    choose one memory access ('p') which alignment you want to force by doing
    1519             :    peeling.  Then, either (1) generate a loop in which 'p' is aligned and all
    1520             :    other accesses are not necessarily aligned, or (2) use loop versioning to
    1521             :    generate one loop in which all accesses are aligned, and another loop in
    1522             :    which only 'p' is necessarily aligned.
    1523             : 
    1524             :    ("Automatic Intra-Register Vectorization for the Intel Architecture",
    1525             :    Aart J.C. Bik, Milind Girkar, Paul M. Grey and Ximmin Tian, International
    1526             :    Journal of Parallel Programming, Vol. 30, No. 2, April 2002.)
    1527             : 
    1528             :    Devising a cost model is the most critical aspect of this work.  It will
    1529             :    guide us on which access to peel for, whether to use loop versioning, how
    1530             :    many versions to create, etc.  The cost model will probably consist of
    1531             :    generic considerations as well as target specific considerations (on
    1532             :    powerpc for example, misaligned stores are more painful than misaligned
    1533             :    loads).
    1534             : 
    1535             :    Here are the general steps involved in alignment enhancements:
    1536             : 
    1537             :      -- original loop, before alignment analysis:
    1538             :         for (i=0; i<N; i++){
    1539             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = unknown
    1540             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = unknown
    1541             :         }
    1542             : 
    1543             :      -- After vect_compute_data_refs_alignment:
    1544             :         for (i=0; i<N; i++){
    1545             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 3
    1546             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = unknown
    1547             :         }
    1548             : 
    1549             :      -- Possibility 1: we do loop versioning:
    1550             :      if (p is aligned) {
    1551             :         for (i=0; i<N; i++){ # loop 1A
    1552             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 3
    1553             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = 0
    1554             :         }
    1555             :      }
    1556             :      else {
    1557             :         for (i=0; i<N; i++){ # loop 1B
    1558             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 3
    1559             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = unaligned
    1560             :         }
    1561             :      }
    1562             : 
    1563             :      -- Possibility 2: we do loop peeling:
    1564             :      for (i = 0; i < 3; i++){        # (scalar loop, not to be vectorized).
    1565             :         x = q[i];
    1566             :         p[i] = y;
    1567             :      }
    1568             :      for (i = 3; i < N; i++){        # loop 2A
    1569             :         x = q[i];                       # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 0
    1570             :         p[i] = y;                       # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = unknown
    1571             :      }
    1572             : 
    1573             :      -- Possibility 3: combination of loop peeling and versioning:
    1574             :      for (i = 0; i < 3; i++){        # (scalar loop, not to be vectorized).
    1575             :         x = q[i];
    1576             :         p[i] = y;
    1577             :      }
    1578             :      if (p is aligned) {
    1579             :         for (i = 3; i<N; i++){       # loop 3A
    1580             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 0
    1581             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = 0
    1582             :         }
    1583             :      }
    1584             :      else {
    1585             :         for (i = 3; i<N; i++){       # loop 3B
    1586             :           x = q[i];                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(q) = 0
    1587             :           p[i] = y;                     # DR_MISALIGNMENT(p) = unaligned
    1588             :         }
    1589             :      }
    1590             : 
    1591             :      These loops are later passed to loop_transform to be vectorized.  The
    1592             :      vectorizer will use the alignment information to guide the transformation
    1593             :      (whether to generate regular loads/stores, or with special handling for
    1594             :      misalignment).  */
    1595             :

    4339             : /* Function vect_create_addr_base_for_vector_ref.
    4340             : 
    4341             :    Create an expression that computes the address of the first memory location
    4342             :    that will be accessed for a data reference.
    4343             : 
    4344             :    Input:
    4345             :    STMT_INFO: The statement containing the data reference.
    4346             :    NEW_STMT_LIST: Must be initialized to NULL_TREE or a statement list.
    4347             :    OFFSET: Optional. If supplied, it is be added to the initial address.
    4348             :    LOOP:    Specify relative to which loop-nest should the address be computed.
    4349             :             For example, when the dataref is in an inner-loop nested in an
    4350             :             outer-loop that is now being vectorized, LOOP can be either the
    4351             :             outer-loop, or the inner-loop.  The first memory location accessed
    4352             :             by the following dataref ('in' points to short):
    4353             : 
    4354             :                 for (i=0; i<N; i++)
    4355             :                    for (j=0; j<M; j++)
    4356             :                      s += in[i+j]
    4357             : 
    4358             :             is as follows:
    4359             :             if LOOP=i_loop:     &in         (relative to i_loop)
    4360             :             if LOOP=j_loop:     &in+i*2B    (relative to j_loop)
    4361             :    BYTE_OFFSET: Optional, defaulted to NULL.  If supplied, it is added to the
    4362             :             initial address.  Unlike OFFSET, which is number of elements to
    4363             :             be added, BYTE_OFFSET is measured in bytes.
    4364             : 
    4365             :    Output:
    4366             :    1. Return an SSA_NAME whose value is the address of the memory location of
    4367             :       the first vector of the data reference.
    4368             :    2. If new_stmt_list is not NULL_TREE after return then the caller must insert
    4369             :       these statement(s) which define the returned SSA_NAME.
    4370             : 
    4371             :    FORNOW: We are only handling array accesses with step 1.  */

    4458             :    Also set aliasing information for the pointer.  This pointer is used by
    4459             :    the callers to this function to create a memory reference expression for
    4460             :    vector load/store access.
    4461             : 
    4462             :    Input:
    4463             :    1. STMT_INFO: a stmt that references memory. Expected to be of the form
    4464             :          GIMPLE_ASSIGN <name, data-ref> or
    4465             :          GIMPLE_ASSIGN <data-ref, name>.
    4466             :    2. AGGR_TYPE: the type of the reference, which should be either a vector
    4467             :         or an array.
    4468             :    3. AT_LOOP: the loop where the vector memref is to be created.
    4469             :    4. OFFSET (optional): an offset to be added to the initial address accessed
    4470             :         by the data-ref in STMT_INFO.
    4471             :    5. BSI: location where the new stmts are to be placed if there is no loop
    4472             :    6. ONLY_INIT: indicate if ap is to be updated in the loop, or remain
    4473             :         pointing to the initial address.
    4474             :    7. BYTE_OFFSET (optional, defaults to NULL): a byte offset to be added
    4475             :         to the initial address accessed by the data-ref in STMT_INFO.  This is
    4476             :         similar to OFFSET, but OFFSET is counted in elements, while BYTE_OFFSET
    4477             :         in bytes.
    4478             :    8. IV_STEP (optional, defaults to NULL): the amount that should be added
    4479             :         to the IV during each iteration of the loop.  NULL says to move
    4480             :         by one copy of AGGR_TYPE up or down, depending on the step of the
    4481             :         data reference.
    4482             : 
    4483             :    Output:
    4484             :    1. Declare a new ptr to vector_type, and have it point to the base of the
    4485             :       data reference (initial addressed accessed by the data reference).
    4486             :       For example, for vector of type V8HI, the following code is generated:
    4487             : 
    4488             :       v8hi *ap;
    4489             :       ap = (v8hi *)initial_address;
    4490             : 
    4491             :       if OFFSET is not supplied:
    4492             :          initial_address = &a[init];
    4493             :       if OFFSET is supplied:
    4494             :          initial_address = &a[init + OFFSET];
    4495             :       if BYTE_OFFSET is supplied:
    4496             :          initial_address = &a[init] + BYTE_OFFSET;
    4497             : 
    4498             :       Return the initial_address in INITIAL_ADDRESS.
    4499             : 
    4500             :    2. If ONLY_INIT is true, just return the initial pointer.  Otherwise, also
    4501             :       update the pointer in each iteration of the loop.
    4502             : 
    4503             :       Return the increment stmt that updates the pointer in PTR_INCR.
    4504             : 
    4505             :    3. Return the pointer.  */

    5009             : /* Function vect_permute_store_chain.
    5010             : 
    5011             :    Given a chain of interleaved stores in DR_CHAIN of LENGTH that must be
    5012             :    a power of 2 or equal to 3, generate interleave_high/low stmts to reorder
    5013             :    the data correctly for the stores.  Return the final references for stores
    5014             :    in RESULT_CHAIN.
    5015             : 
    5016             :    E.g., LENGTH is 4 and the scalar type is short, i.e., VF is 8.
    5017             :    The input is 4 vectors each containing 8 elements.  We assign a number to
    5018             :    each element, the input sequence is:
    5019             : 
    5020             :    1st vec:   0  1  2  3  4  5  6  7
    5021             :    2nd vec:   8  9 10 11 12 13 14 15
    5022             :    3rd vec:  16 17 18 19 20 21 22 23
    5023             :    4th vec:  24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31
    5024             : 
    5025             :    The output sequence should be:
    5026             : 
    5027             :    1st vec:  0  8 16 24  1  9 17 25
    5028             :    2nd vec:  2 10 18 26  3 11 19 27
    5029             :    3rd vec:  4 12 20 28  5 13 21 30
    5030             :    4th vec:  6 14 22 30  7 15 23 31
    5031             : 
    5032             :    i.e., we interleave the contents of the four vectors in their order.
    5033             : 
    5034             :    We use interleave_high/low instructions to create such output.  The input of
    5035             :    each interleave_high/low operation is two vectors:
    5036             :    1st vec    2nd vec
    5037             :    0 1 2 3    4 5 6 7
    5038             :    the even elements of the result vector are obtained left-to-right from the
    5039             :    high/low elements of the first vector.  The odd elements of the result are
    5040             :    obtained left-to-right from the high/low elements of the second vector.
    5041             :    The output of interleave_high will be:   0 4 1 5
    5042             :    and of interleave_low:                   2 6 3 7
    5043             : 
    5044             : 
    5045             :    The permutation is done in log LENGTH stages.  In each stage interleave_high
    5046             :    and interleave_low stmts are created for each pair of vectors in DR_CHAIN,
    5047             :    where the first argument is taken from the first half of DR_CHAIN and the
    5048             :    second argument from it's second half.
    5049             :    In our example,
    5050             : 
    5051             :    I1: interleave_high (1st vec, 3rd vec)
    5052             :    I2: interleave_low (1st vec, 3rd vec)
    5053             :    I3: interleave_high (2nd vec, 4th vec)
    5054             :    I4: interleave_low (2nd vec, 4th vec)
    5055             : 
    5056             :    The output for the first stage is:
    5057             : 
    5058             :    I1:  0 16  1 17  2 18  3 19
    5059             :    I2:  4 20  5 21  6 22  7 23
    5060             :    I3:  8 24  9 25 10 26 11 27
    5061             :    I4: 12 28 13 29 14 30 15 31
    5062             : 
    5063             :    The output of the second stage, i.e. the final result is:
    5064             : 
    5065             :    I1:  0  8 16 24  1  9 17 25
    5066             :    I2:  2 10 18 26  3 11 19 27
    5067             :    I3:  4 12 20 28  5 13 21 30
    5068             :    I4:  6 14 22 30  7 15 23 31.  */

    5207             : /* Function vect_setup_realignment
    5208             : 
    5209             :    This function is called when vectorizing an unaligned load using
    5210             :    the dr_explicit_realign[_optimized] scheme.
    5211             :    This function generates the following code at the loop prolog:
    5212             : 
    5213             :       p = initial_addr;
    5214             :    x  msq_init = *(floor(p));   # prolog load
    5215             :       realignment_token = call target_builtin;
    5216             :     loop:
    5217             :    x  msq = phi (msq_init, ---)
    5218             : 
    5219             :    The stmts marked with x are generated only for the case of
    5220             :    dr_explicit_realign_optimized.
    5221             : 
    5222             :    The code above sets up a new (vector) pointer, pointing to the first
    5223             :    location accessed by STMT_INFO, and a "floor-aligned" load using that
    5224             :    pointer.  It also generates code to compute the "realignment-token"
    5225             :    (if the relevant target hook was defined), and creates a phi-node at the
    5226             :    loop-header bb whose arguments are the result of the prolog-load (created
    5227             :    by this function) and the result of a load that takes place in the loop
    5228             :    (to be created by the caller to this function).
    5229             : 
    5230             :    For the case of dr_explicit_realign_optimized:
    5231             :    The caller to this function uses the phi-result (msq) to create the
    5232             :    realignment code inside the loop, and sets up the missing phi argument,
    5233             :    as follows:
    5234             :     loop:
    5235             :       msq = phi (msq_init, lsq)
    5236             :       lsq = *(floor(p'));        # load in loop
    5237             :       result = realign_load (msq, lsq, realignment_token);
    5238             : 
    5239             :    For the case of dr_explicit_realign:
    5240             :     loop:
    5241             :       msq = *(floor(p));        # load in loop
    5242             :       p' = p + (VS-1);
    5243             :       lsq = *(floor(p'));       # load in loop
    5244             :       result = realign_load (msq, lsq, realignment_token);
    5245             : 
    5246             :    Input:
    5247             :    STMT_INFO - (scalar) load stmt to be vectorized. This load accesses
    5248             :                a memory location that may be unaligned.
    5249             :    BSI - place where new code is to be inserted.
    5250             :    ALIGNMENT_SUPPORT_SCHEME - which of the two misalignment handling schemes
    5251             :                               is used.
    5252             : 
    5253             :    Output:
    5254             :    REALIGNMENT_TOKEN - the result of a call to the builtin_mask_for_load
    5255             :                        target hook, if defined.
    5256             :    Return value - the result of the loop-header phi node.  */

    5304             :      If INIT_ADDR is NULL_TREE, this indicates that the misalignment
    5305             :      calculation will be generated by this function, outside the loop (in the
    5306             :      preheader).  Otherwise, INIT_ADDR had already been computed for us by the

    5309             :      Background: If the misalignment remains fixed throughout the iterations of
    5310             :      the loop, then both realignment schemes are applicable, and also the
    5311             :      misalignment computation can be done outside LOOP.  This is because we are
    5312             :      vectorizing LOOP, and so the memory accesses in LOOP advance in steps that
    5313             :      are a multiple of VS (the Vector Size), and therefore the misalignment in
    5314             :      different vectorized LOOP iterations is always the same.
    5315             :      The problem arises only if the memory access is in an inner-loop nested
    5316             :      inside LOOP, which is now being vectorized using outer-loop vectorization.
    5317             :      This is the only case when the misalignment of the memory access may not
    5318             :      remain fixed throughout the iterations of the inner-loop (as explained in
    5319             :      detail in vect_supportable_dr_alignment).  In this case, not only is the
    5320             :      optimized realignment scheme not applicable, but also the misalignment
    5321             :      computation (and generation of the realignment token that is passed to
    5322             :      REALIGN_LOAD) have to be done inside the loop.
    5323             : 
    5324             :      In short, INIT_ADDR indicates whether we are in a COMPUTE_IN_LOOP mode
    5325             :      or not, which in turn determines if the misalignment is computed inside

    5335             :   /* 2. Determine where to generate the extra vector load.
    5336             : 
    5337             :      For the optimized realignment scheme, instead of generating two vector
    5338             :      loads in each iteration, we generate a single extra vector load in the
    5339             :      preheader of the loop, and in each iteration reuse the result of the
    5340             :      vector load from the previous iteration.  In case the memory access is in

    5613             : /* Function vect_permute_load_chain.
    5614             : 
    5615             :    Given a chain of interleaved loads in DR_CHAIN of LENGTH that must be
    5616             :    a power of 2 or equal to 3, generate extract_even/odd stmts to reorder
    5617             :    the input data correctly.  Return the final references for loads in
    5618             :    RESULT_CHAIN.
    5619             : 
    5620             :    E.g., LENGTH is 4 and the scalar type is short, i.e., VF is 8.
    5621             :    The input is 4 vectors each containing 8 elements. We assign a number to each
    5622             :    element, the input sequence is:
    5623             : 
    5624             :    1st vec:   0  1  2  3  4  5  6  7
    5625             :    2nd vec:   8  9 10 11 12 13 14 15
    5626             :    3rd vec:  16 17 18 19 20 21 22 23
    5627             :    4th vec:  24 25 26 27 28 29 30 31
    5628             : 
    5629             :    The output sequence should be:
    5630             : 
    5631             :    1st vec:  0 4  8 12 16 20 24 28
    5632             :    2nd vec:  1 5  9 13 17 21 25 29
    5633             :    3rd vec:  2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30
    5634             :    4th vec:  3 7 11 15 19 23 27 31
    5635             : 
    5636             :    i.e., the first output vector should contain the first elements of each
    5637             :    interleaving group, etc.
    5638             : 
    5639             :    We use extract_even/odd instructions to create such output.  The input of
    5640             :    each extract_even/odd operation is two vectors
    5641             :    1st vec    2nd vec
    5642             :    0 1 2 3    4 5 6 7
    5643             : 
    5644             :    and the output is the vector of extracted even/odd elements.  The output of
    5645             :    extract_even will be:   0 2 4 6
    5646             :    and of extract_odd:     1 3 5 7
    5647             : 
    5648             : 
    5649             :    The permutation is done in log LENGTH stages.  In each stage extract_even
    5650             :    and extract_odd stmts are created for each pair of vectors in DR_CHAIN in
    5651             :    their order.  In our example,
    5652             : 
    5653             :    E1: extract_even (1st vec, 2nd vec)
    5654             :    E2: extract_odd (1st vec, 2nd vec)
    5655             :    E3: extract_even (3rd vec, 4th vec)
    5656             :    E4: extract_odd (3rd vec, 4th vec)
    5657             : 
    5658             :    The output for the first stage will be:
    5659             : 
    5660             :    E1:  0  2  4  6  8 10 12 14
    5661             :    E2:  1  3  5  7  9 11 13 15
    5662             :    E3: 16 18 20 22 24 26 28 30
    5663             :    E4: 17 19 21 23 25 27 29 31
    5664             : 
    5665             :    In order to proceed and create the correct sequence for the next stage (or
    5666             :    for the correct output, if the second stage is the last one, as in our
    5667             :    example), we first put the output of extract_even operation and then the
    5668             :    output of extract_odd in RESULT_CHAIN (which is then copied to DR_CHAIN).
    5669             :    The input for the second stage is:
    5670             : 
    5671             :    1st vec (E1):  0  2  4  6  8 10 12 14
    5672             :    2nd vec (E3): 16 18 20 22 24 26 28 30
    5673             :    3rd vec (E2):  1  3  5  7  9 11 13 15
    5674             :    4th vec (E4): 17 19 21 23 25 27 29 31
    5675             : 
    5676             :    The output of the second stage:
    5677             : 
    5678             :    E1: 0 4  8 12 16 20 24 28
    5679             :    E2: 2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30
    5680             :    E3: 1 5  9 13 17 21 25 29
    5681             :    E4: 3 7 11 15 19 23 27 31
    5682             : 
    5683             :    And RESULT_CHAIN after reordering:
    5684             : 
    5685             :    1st vec (E1):  0 4  8 12 16 20 24 28
    5686             :    2nd vec (E3):  1 5  9 13 17 21 25 29
    5687             :    3rd vec (E2):  2 6 10 14 18 22 26 30
    5688             :    4th vec (E4):  3 7 11 15 19 23 27 31.  */
    5689             :

    5805             : 
    5806             : /* Function vect_shift_permute_load_chain.
    5807             : 
    5808             :    Given a chain of loads in DR_CHAIN of LENGTH 2 or 3, generate
    5809             :    sequence of stmts to reorder the input data accordingly.
    5810             :    Return the final references for loads in RESULT_CHAIN.
    5811             :    Return true if successed, false otherwise.
    5812             : 
    5813             :    E.g., LENGTH is 3 and the scalar type is short, i.e., VF is 8.
    5814             :    The input is 3 vectors each containing 8 elements.  We assign a
    5815             :    number to each element, the input sequence is:
    5816             : 
    5817             :    1st vec:   0  1  2  3  4  5  6  7
    5818             :    2nd vec:   8  9 10 11 12 13 14 15
    5819             :    3rd vec:  16 17 18 19 20 21 22 23
    5820             : 
    5821             :    The output sequence should be:
    5822             : 
    5823             :    1st vec:  0 3 6  9 12 15 18 21
    5824             :    2nd vec:  1 4 7 10 13 16 19 22
    5825             :    3rd vec:  2 5 8 11 14 17 20 23
    5826             : 
    5827             :    We use 3 shuffle instructions and 3 * 3 - 1 shifts to create such output.
    5828             : 
    5829             :    First we shuffle all 3 vectors to get correct elements order:
    5830             : 
    5831             :    1st vec:  ( 0  3  6) ( 1  4  7) ( 2  5)
    5832             :    2nd vec:  ( 8 11 14) ( 9 12 15) (10 13)
    5833             :    3rd vec:  (16 19 22) (17 20 23) (18 21)
    5834             : 
    5835             :    Next we unite and shift vector 3 times:
    5836             : 
    5837             :    1st step:
    5838             :      shift right by 6 the concatenation of:
    5839             :      "1st vec" and  "2nd vec"
    5840             :        ( 0  3  6) ( 1  4  7) |( 2  5) _ ( 8 11 14) ( 9 12 15)| (10 13)
    5841             :      "2nd vec" and  "3rd vec"
    5842             :        ( 8 11 14) ( 9 12 15) |(10 13) _ (16 19 22) (17 20 23)| (18 21)
    5843             :      "3rd vec" and  "1st vec"
    5844             :        (16 19 22) (17 20 23) |(18 21) _ ( 0  3  6) ( 1  4  7)| ( 2  5)
    5845             :                              | New vectors                   |
    5846             : 
    5847             :      So that now new vectors are:
    5848             : 
    5849             :      1st vec:  ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14) ( 9 12 15)
    5850             :      2nd vec:  (10 13) (16 19 22) (17 20 23)
    5851             :      3rd vec:  (18 21) ( 0  3  6) ( 1  4  7)
    5852             : 
    5853             :    2nd step:
    5854             :      shift right by 5 the concatenation of:
    5855             :      "1st vec" and  "3rd vec"
    5856             :        ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14) |( 9 12 15) _ (18 21) ( 0  3  6)| ( 1  4  7)
    5857             :      "2nd vec" and  "1st vec"
    5858             :        (10 13) (16 19 22) |(17 20 23) _ ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14)| ( 9 12 15)
    5859             :      "3rd vec" and  "2nd vec"
    5860             :        (18 21) ( 0  3  6) |( 1  4  7) _ (10 13) (16 19 22)| (17 20 23)
    5861             :                           | New vectors                   |
    5862             : 
    5863             :      So that now new vectors are:
    5864             : 
    5865             :      1st vec:  ( 9 12 15) (18 21) ( 0  3  6)
    5866             :      2nd vec:  (17 20 23) ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14)
    5867             :      3rd vec:  ( 1  4  7) (10 13) (16 19 22) READY
    5868             : 
    5869             :    3rd step:
    5870             :      shift right by 5 the concatenation of:
    5871             :      "1st vec" and  "1st vec"
    5872             :        ( 9 12 15) (18 21) |( 0  3  6) _ ( 9 12 15) (18 21)| ( 0  3  6)
    5873             :      shift right by 3 the concatenation of:
    5874             :      "2nd vec" and  "2nd vec"
    5875             :                (17 20 23) |( 2  5) ( 8 11 14) _ (17 20 23)| ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14)
    5876             :                           | New vectors                   |
    5877             : 
    5878             :      So that now all vectors are READY:
    5879             :      1st vec:  ( 0  3  6) ( 9 12 15) (18 21)
    5880             :      2nd vec:  ( 2  5) ( 8 11 14) (17 20 23)
    5881             :      3rd vec:  ( 1  4  7) (10 13) (16 19 22)
    5882             : 
    5883             :    This algorithm is faster than one in vect_permute_load_chain if:
    5884             :      1.  "shift of a concatination" is faster than general permutation.
    5885             :          This is usually so.
    5886             :      2.  The TARGET machine can't execute vector instructions in parallel.
    5887             :          This is because each step of the algorithm depends on previous.
    5888             :          The algorithm in vect_permute_load_chain is much more parallel.
    5889             : 
    5890             :    The algorithm is applicable only for LOAD CHAIN LENGTH less than VF.
    5891             : */
    5892             :

    6319             :   /* We can choose between using the implicit realignment scheme (generating
    6320             :      a misaligned_move stmt) and the explicit realignment scheme (generating
    6321             :      aligned loads with a REALIGN_LOAD).  There are two variants to the
    6322             :      explicit realignment scheme: optimized, and unoptimized.
    6323             :      We can optimize the realignment only if the step between consecutive
    6324             :      vector loads is equal to the vector size.  Since the vector memory
    6325             :      accesses advance in steps of VS (Vector Size) in the vectorized loop, it
    6326             :      is guaranteed that the misalignment amount remains the same throughout the
    6327             :      execution of the vectorized loop.  Therefore, we can create the
    6328             :      "realignment token" (the permutation mask that is passed to REALIGN_LOAD)
    6329             :      at the loop preheader.
    6330             : 
    6331             :      However, in the case of outer-loop vectorization, when vectorizing a
    6332             :      memory access in the inner-loop nested within the LOOP that is now being
    6333             :      vectorized, while it is guaranteed that the misalignment of the
    6334             :      vectorized memory access will remain the same in different outer-loop
    6335             :      iterations, it is *not* guaranteed that is will remain the same throughout
    6336             :      the execution of the inner-loop.  This is because the inner-loop advances
    6337             :      with the original scalar step (and not in steps of VS).  If the inner-loop
    6338             :      step happens to be a multiple of VS, then the misalignment remains fixed
    6339             :      and we can use the optimized realignment scheme.  For example:
    6340             : 
    6341             :       for (i=0; i<N; i++)
    6342             :         for (j=0; j<M; j++)
    6343             :           s += a[i+j];
    6344             : 
    6345             :      When vectorizing the i-loop in the above example, the step between
    6346             :      consecutive vector loads is 1, and so the misalignment does not remain

    6348             :      be optimized (as illustrated in the following pseudo vectorized loop):

    6350             :       for (i=0; i<N; i+=4)

    6353             :                          // when j is {0,1,2,3,4,5,6,7,...} respectively.
    6354             :                          // (assuming that we start from an aligned address).
    6355             :           }
    6356             : 
    6357             :      We therefore have to use the unoptimized realignment scheme:
    6358             : 
    6359             :       for (i=0; i<N; i+=4)
    6360             :           for (j=k; j<M; j+=4)
